        </div><div class="casAbstract">Severe safety concerns are impeding the large-scale employment of lithium/sodium batteries.  Conventional electrolytes are highly flammable and volatile, which may cause catastrophic fires or explosions.  Efforts to introduce flame-retardant solvents into the electrolytes have generally resulted in compromised battery performance because those solvents do not suitably passivate carbonaceous anodes.  Here we report a salt-concd. electrolyte design to resolve this dilemma via the spontaneous formation of a robust inorg. passivation film on the anode.  We demonstrate that a concd. electrolyte using a salt and a popular flame-retardant solvent (tri-Me phosphate), without any additives or soft binders, allows stable charge-discharge cycling of both hard-carbon and graphite anodes for more than 1,000 cycles (over one year) with negligible degrdn.; this performance is comparable or superior to that of conventional flammable carbonate electrolytes.  The unusual passivation character of the concd. electrolyte coupled with its fire-extinguishing property contributes to developing safe and long-lasting batteries, unlocking the limit toward development of much higher energy-d. batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqh5VD_9omOWrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhqMszPvXWBNw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitVehtbc%253D&amp;md5=f17e94b071fcc675467c969b0b2e28ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1149/1945-7111/ab75fd"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fondard, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Irisarri, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Courrèges, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacin, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium ion battery (NIB) is a promising alternative technol. for energy storage systems because of the abundance and low cost of sodium in the Earth's crust.  However, the limited cycle life and safety concerns of NIBs hinder their large-scale applications.  Here, we report a nonflammable localized high concn. electrolyte (sodium bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide-triethyl phosphate/1,1,2,2-tetrafluoroethyl-2,2,3,3-tetrafluoropropyl ether (1:1.5:2 in molar ratio)) for highly reversible NIBs. These stable interphases enabled high Coulombic efficiency and long-term stable cycling of the HC anode and the NaCu1/9Ni2/9Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode. High-concn. electrolytes (HCE, ≥4 M) consisting of sodium bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide (NaFSI) and ether solvent could ensure the stable cycling of Na metal with high Coulombic efficiency but at the cost of high viscosity, poor wettability, and high salt cost.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Anode-free lithium-metal batteries (LMBs) are ideal candidates for high-capacity energy storage as they eliminate the need for a conventional graphite electrode or excess lithium-metal anode.  Current anode-free LMBs suffer from low Coulombic efficiency (CE) due to poor lithium stripping efficiency.  Advanced electrolyte development is a promising route to maximize lithium plating and stripping CE and minimize capacity fade.  However, a poor understanding of the mechanisms by which advanced electrolytes improve performance hampers progress in the practical development of anode-free LMBs.  Here, we use synchrotron techniques and other tools to analyze the influence of three com. available electrolytes on the compn., heterogeneity, kinetics, morphol., and electrochem. of anode-free LMBs. Li plates uniformly over the electrode area with the advanced electrolytes rather than in a few active sites.  Inactive cryst. Li with heterogeneous distribution dominates the capacity degrdn. of anode-free cells, esp. with the conventional electrolyte, indicating that reducing the amt. of "dead" cryst. Li will significantly improve the cycling stability of anode-free cells. However, EC is highly susceptible to oxidn. on the surface of high-nickel layered oxide cathodes, making it undesirable for next-generation high-energy-d. LIBs.  In this study, a simple, yet effective, EC-free electrolyte (20F1.5M-1TDI) is presented by adding 20 wt% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) and 1 wt% lithium 4,5-dicyano-2-(trifluoromethyl)imidazole (LiTDI) into 1.5 M LiPF6 in an Et Me carbonate (EMC) electrolyte.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cathode materials control both the energy d. and cost of Li-ion and Li-metal batteries.  The cobalt-free LiNiO2 with relatively low cost and extremely high theor. energy d. (∼1,050 Wh kg-1) is one of the most promising cathode materials for high-energy batteries. Here, we surmount these challenges by forming a robust fluoride (F)- and boron (B)-rich CEI on LiNiO2 using a high-fluorinated electrolyte with LiDFOB additive.         </div><div class="casAbstract">LiNiO2 (LNO) is a high-capacity and model cathode first discovered in the 1980s that fell out of favor due to its intrinsic instabilities.  However, research activities toward LNO are once again on the rise as the push for higher-energy-d. cells marches on.  We demonstrate here that with appropriate modern electrolytes, major performance improvements can be achieved with LNO with no addnl. modifications.  Cells with a localized high concn. electrolyte (LHCE) deliver 92% capacity retention after 200 cycles compared with 56% capacity retention in a baseline carbonate electrolyte, maintain 94% capacity after high-voltage storage compared with 77% capacity, and display a higher onset temp. of thermal runaway of 244°C compared with 188°C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Interest in sodium-ion battery cathode materials, particularly for grid-scale energy-storage applications, has considerably increased in the last few years, sparking a push toward industrially practical research.  In addn. to more full-cell and pouch-cell research, there has also been more study on the use of an industrial synthesis technique for producing sodium-based cathode materials.  Hydroxide copptn. is the industry std. for synthesizing lithium-based layered-oxide cathode materials because it is scalable and produces materials with highly tunable particle morphol. with low impurity.  The tuning of particle morphol. allows for improved energy d. and reduced surface reactivity, leading to better stability in air and electrolyte.  Despite these benefits, the ability to synthesize sodium-based layered-oxide cathode materials with beneficial particle morphol. is considerably more challenging than it is for lithium-based layered oxides due to the complexity of numerous interconnected variables.  We herein provide a review of the hydroxide copptn. method for both sodium- and lithium-based cathode materials, highlighting its benefits and the need for further studies on utilizing copptd. sodium-based layered-oxide materials.  We then perform an in-depth anal. utilizing a combination of literature, fundamental chem., and exptl. data to discuss the challenges of hydroxide copptn. and provide a framework for overcoming these challenges.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGosifkOzKyUyLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAL3m3L6gvEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVeisrzJ&amp;md5=5edfe0970f6fb50b5f2486e7abf823d0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.08.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Che, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.-F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Long Cycle Life of Sodium-Ion Pouch Cell Achieved by Using Multiple Electrolyte Additives</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>407</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">173</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">179</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.08.025</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Long cycle life of sodium-ion pouch cell achieved by using multiple electrolyte additives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Che, Haiying; Yang, Xinrong; Wang, Hong; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; Zhang, Sheng S.; Wang, Chunsheng; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">407</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">173-179</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion pouch cells with up to 1000 cycles are presented by using a NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode, a hard carbon anode, and a functional electrolyte.  The functional electrolyte is composed of 1 M NaPF6 dissolved in a 1:1 (vol./vol.) mixed solvent of propylene carbonate (PC) and Et Me carbonate (EMC) with 3-4 wt% of two or three additives, including fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC), prop-1-ene-1,3-sultone (PST), and 1,3,2-Dioxathiolane-2,2-dioxide (DTD).  It is shown that the capacity retentions of the cells increase to 84.4% and 92.2% after 1000 cycles for electrolytes contg. FEC-PST bi-additive and FEC-PST-DTD tri-additive, resp., as compared with that contg. FEC single additive.  Using XPS, inductively coupled plasma optical, and transmission electron microscopy, post-mortem analyses on the surface of the cycled electrodes indicate that PST and DTD are beneficial to the anode by forming an org. compd. rich solid electrolyte interphase (SEI), and to the cathode by forming a dense and thick cathode electrolyte interphase (CEI) that consequently prevents transition metal ions from dissolving into electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-8YJtx9tWOLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAL3m3L6gvEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhsFahtLnI&amp;md5=5fc47b41d2211cc84d4e027d0f0b8670</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpcc.7b12140"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Quaternary Transition Metal Oxide Layered Framework: O3-Type Na[Ni <sub>0.32</sub> Fe <sub>0.13</sub> Co <sub>0.15</sub> Mn <sub>0.40</sub> ]O <sub>2</sub> Cathode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Phys. Chem. C</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>122</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13500</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13507</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.jpcc.7b12140</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quaternary Transition Metal Oxide Layered Framework: O3-Type Na[Ni0.32Fe0.13Co0.15Mn0.40]O2 Cathode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">122</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13500-13507</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Analogous compds. in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), various ternary chem. compns. in O3-type layered oxides, have been introduced in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, O3-type ternary transition metal oxide cathodes, including the NaNixCoyMnzO2 and NaNixFeyMnzO2 (x + y + z = 1) compds., continue to face several challenges with respect to their low reversible capacity and poor cycle retention owing to their structural instability.  Herein, we propose the well-balanced quaternary transition metal oxide structure of O3-type Na[Ni0.32Fe0.13Co0.15Mn0.40]O2 as cathode materials that have an av. compn. of both Na[Ni0.25Fe0.25Mn0.5]O2 and Na[Ni0.4Co0.3Mn0.3]O2 compds.  Compared to its resp. ternary members, the Na[Ni0.32Fe0.13Co0.15Mn0.40]O2 cathode exhibits a higher specific capacity as well as improved cycling stability and rate capability.  The post-mortem ex-situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) studies of a cycled electrode clearly show that coexistence of quaternary transition metals in a Na[Ni0.32Fe0.13Co0.15Mn0.40]O2 cathode could improve the structural stability.  Moreover, quaternary transition metal oxide frameworks effectively prevent the dissoln. of transition metals during cycling, thus improving the battery performances.  The appealing phys. properties and electrochem. performance of this material demonstrate its great promise for a high-performance O3-type cathode in sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHbvW6EKdvbbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liAL3m3L6gvEw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXktlGiu74%253D&amp;md5=bee338c33dd75d3de0cf70438e781812</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i8">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.2c05402?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.2c05402</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Further details of the sodium metal SEM and EDX, additional XPS regions, and GITT impedance analysis (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.2c05402/suppl_file/am2c05402_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.2c05402/suppl_file/am2c05402_si_001.pdf">am2c05402_si_001.pdf (802.48 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {

	});

<script nonce="90da89136a85b325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da89136a85b325-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>
